"""Grouped GEMM + fused SwiGLU for MoE up-projection on Ampere (SM86).

Single fused Triton kernel with a sync-free device-side schedule.  From
expert_offsets we build a per-(m-tile) slot table on the GPU; each program
looks up its (expert, row_start) and computes:

    h_e = silu(x_e @ W_gate[e]) * (x_e @ W_up[e])

The same x tile is loaded once and fed into both gate/up dots.
"""
from __future__ import annotations

import os
os.environ.setdefault("PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF", "expandable_segments:True")

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
import triton
import triton.language as tl


@triton.jit
def moe_swiglu_grouped_kernel(
    x_ptr,
    w_gate_ptr,
    w_up_ptr,
    out_ptr,
    expert_offsets_ptr,
    tile_expert_ptr,
    tile_row_start_ptr,
    grid_m,
    T_perm,
    H,
    I,
    stride_xm,
    stride_xk,
    stride_we,
    stride_wk,
    stride_wn,
    stride_om,
    stride_on,
    BLOCK_M: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr,
    BLOCK_K: tl.constexpr,
    GROUP_M: tl.constexpr,
):
    """One fused (m-tile, n-tile) block of grouped GEMM + SwiGLU."""
    pid = tl.program_id(0)
    num_pid_m = grid_m
    num_pid_n = (I + BLOCK_N - 1) // BLOCK_N
    num_pid_in_group = GROUP_M * num_pid_n
    group_id = pid // num_pid_in_group
    first_pid_m = group_id * GROUP_M
    group_size_m = min(num_pid_m - first_pid_m, GROUP_M)
    pid_m = first_pid_m + (pid % group_size_m)
    pid_n = (pid % num_pid_in_group) // group_size_m

    expert = tl.load(tile_expert_ptr + pid_m)
    if expert == -1:
        return

    row_start = tl.load(tile_row_start_ptr + pid_m)
    row_end = tl.load(expert_offsets_ptr + expert + 1)

    offs_m = row_start + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_M)
    offs_n = pid_n * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)

    acc_gate = tl.zeros((BLOCK_M, BLOCK_N), dtype=tl.float32)
    acc_up = tl.zeros((BLOCK_M, BLOCK_N), dtype=tl.float32)

    w_gate_e = w_gate_ptr + expert * stride_we
    w_up_e = w_up_ptr + expert * stride_we

    for k in range(0, tl.cdiv(H, BLOCK_K)):
        offs_k = k * BLOCK_K + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K)
        x_ptrs = x_ptr + (offs_m[:, None] * stride_xm + offs_k[None, :] * stride_xk)
        w_gate_ptrs = w_gate_e + (offs_k[:, None] * stride_wk + offs_n[None, :] * stride_wn)
        w_up_ptrs = w_up_e + (offs_k[:, None] * stride_wk + offs_n[None, :] * stride_wn)

        mask_k = offs_k < H
        mask_m = offs_m < row_end
        mask_n = offs_n < I
        x_block = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask_m[:, None] & mask_k[None, :], other=0.0)
        w_gate_block = tl.load(w_gate_ptrs, mask=mask_k[:, None] & mask_n[None, :], other=0.0)
        w_up_block = tl.load(w_up_ptrs, mask=mask_k[:, None] & mask_n[None, :], other=0.0)

        acc_gate = tl.dot(x_block, w_gate_block, acc_gate)
        acc_up = tl.dot(x_block, w_up_block, acc_up)

    gate = acc_gate.to(tl.bfloat16)
    up = acc_up.to(tl.bfloat16)

    gate_f = gate.to(tl.float32)
    silu = gate_f * tl.sigmoid(gate_f)
    out = (silu * up.to(tl.float32)).to(tl.bfloat16)

    out_ptrs = out_ptr + (offs_m[:, None] * stride_om + offs_n[None, :] * stride_on)
    tl.store(out_ptrs, out, mask=(offs_m[:, None] < row_end) & (offs_n[None, :] < I))


class Model(nn.Module):
    """Up-projection of a top-K MoE FFN with fused SwiGLU.

    Inputs at call time:
      hidden_states:    (T_perm, H)  bf16, already permuted to expert order
      expert_offsets:   (E+1,)       int32, prefix sums of token counts per expert
    Output:
      gated_up:         (T_perm, I)  bf16
    """

    def __init__(self, T_total: int, H: int, I: int, E: int, K: int):  # noqa: E741
        super().__init__()
        self.T_total = T_total
        self.H = H
        self.I = I
        self.E = E
        self.K = K
        self.W_gate = nn.Parameter(torch.empty(E, H, I, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
        self.W_up = nn.Parameter(torch.empty(E, H, I, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
        nn.init.normal_(self.W_gate, std=0.02)
        nn.init.normal_(self.W_up, std=0.02)

    def forward(
        self,
        hidden_states: torch.Tensor,
        expert_offsets: torch.Tensor,
    ) -> torch.Tensor:
        T_perm, H = hidden_states.shape
        I = self.I
        device = hidden_states.device
        out = torch.empty(T_perm, I, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=device)

        BLOCK_M = 128
        BLOCK_N = 64
        BLOCK_K = 64
        GROUP_M = 8

        # ---- sync-free tile schedule on GPU ---------------------------------
        counts = expert_offsets[1:] - expert_offsets[:-1]
        tiles_per_expert = (counts + BLOCK_M - 1) // BLOCK_M
        tile_offsets = torch.cat([
            torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.int32, device=device),
            torch.cumsum(tiles_per_expert, dim=0),
        ])
        grid_m = (T_perm + BLOCK_M - 1) // BLOCK_M + self.E

        tile_idx = torch.arange(grid_m, dtype=torch.int32, device=device)
        tile_expert = torch.searchsorted(tile_offsets, tile_idx, right=True) - 1
        tile_row_start = expert_offsets[tile_expert] + (tile_idx - tile_offsets[tile_expert]) * BLOCK_M
        tile_expert = torch.where(tile_idx < tile_offsets[-1], tile_expert, torch.full_like(tile_expert, -1))

        grid = (grid_m * triton.cdiv(I, BLOCK_N),)
        moe_swiglu_grouped_kernel[grid](
            hidden_states,
            self.W_gate,
            self.W_up,
            out,
            expert_offsets,
            tile_expert,
            tile_row_start,
            grid_m,
            T_perm,
            H,
            I,
            hidden_states.stride(0),
            hidden_states.stride(1),
            self.W_gate.stride(0),
            self.W_gate.stride(1),
            self.W_gate.stride(2),
            out.stride(0),
            out.stride(1),
            BLOCK_M=BLOCK_M,
            BLOCK_N=BLOCK_N,
            BLOCK_K=BLOCK_K,
            GROUP_M=GROUP_M,
            num_warps=4,
            num_stages=2,
        )

        return out
Implemented `solution.py` with a single fused Triton kernel for the grouped GEMM + SwiGLU up-projection on RTX 3090 (SM86). What it does: - Builds a sync-free device-side tile schedule from `expert_offsets` using `torch.searchsorted` (no `.cpu()`/`.item()` syncs). - Launches one kernel covering all `(m-tile, n-tile)` slots; padded slots early-return via `expert == -1`. - Each block loads one `x` tile and feeds it into both gate and up `tl.dot` accumulators (fp32 acc), then fuses `silu(gate) * up` in the epilogue with bf16 round-trips matching PyTorch semantics. - Sets `PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF=expandable_segments:True` at import time to avoid the `check.py` OOM fragmentation issue on the 24 GB card. Verified: - `uv run python check.py` → `PASS` - `uv run python benchmark.py` → `peak_fraction: 0.1610`, `RESULT: OK` Per-shape results: - shape 0 (32K/4096/1536/128/8): 9.54 TFLOPS, 0.1344 peak fraction - shape 1 (4K/2048/1024/64/4): 16.43 TFLOPS, 0.2314 peak fraction - shape 2 (16K/2048/4096/64/8): 9.53 TFLOPS, 0.1342 peak fraction Tuned config: `BLOCK_M=128`, `BLOCK_N=64`, `BLOCK_K=64`, `GROUP_M=8`, `num_warps=4`, `num_stages=2`.

1	"""Naive grouped GEMM + fused SwiGLU reference (correctness only, NOT the SOTA).
2	
3	This is the up-projection of an MoE FFN. Each token i is assigned to K experts;
4	expert_indices[i*K + j] tells you which expert. Tokens are dispatched to experts
5	according to routing metadata; we compute, per expert e:
6	
7	    h_e = silu(x_e @ W_gate[e])  *  (x_e @ W_up[e])
8	
9	where x_e is the slice of permuted hidden states routed to expert e, with
10	expert_offsets[e]:expert_offsets[e+1] giving its row range in the permuted layout.
11

stdout (1970 chars) — TRUNCATED
1	name: 06_sonic_moe_swiglu
2	display_name: "Sonic-MoE up-projection (Grouped GEMM + SwiGLU)"
3	precision: bf16
4	regime: compute
5	hardware: [RTX_3090]
6	peak_tflops_key: bf16
7	peak_bandwidth_key: dram
8	
9	# Dense-equivalent FLOPs: gate GEMM + up GEMM + SwiGLU (negligible elementwise).
10	# Per token: 2*H*I FMAs for gate, 2*H*I for up => 2 * T_total * H * (2*I).
11	# (Each of T_total tokens visits K experts, but total work = T_total * K * (2*H*I*2)
12	# only if you count routing. The standard MoE FLOPs convention counts only the
13	# active per-token compute: T_total tokens * 2 * (2*I) * H. We follow that.)
14	flops_formula: "2 * T_total * H * (2 * I)"
15	
16	# Bytes moved (approximate, lower bound):
17	#   read hidden (T_perm = T_total*K rows of H bf16) + read 2 weight matrices per
18	#   expert (E * H * 2*I bf16) + write output (T_perm rows of I bf16).
19	bytes_formula: "T_total*K*H*2 + E*H*(2*I)*2 + T_total*K*I*2"
20	
21	tolerance:
22	  bfloat16: 0.02

1	"""Roofline math: achieved TFLOPS / GB/s, peak fraction.
2	
3	FLOPS and bytes formulas come from the problem's `problem.yaml`. They are the
4	dense-equivalent algorithmic work; kernels that skip work (sparsity, early
5	exit) are still measured against the dense cost.
6	"""
7	from __future__ import annotations
8	
9	
10	def compute_tflops(flops: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
11	    """flops per invocation and wall time in ms -> TFLOPS."""
12	    if time_ms <= 0:
13	        return 0.0
14	    return flops / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e12
15	
16	
17	def compute_gbps(bytes_moved: float, time_ms: float) -> float:
18	    """bytes per invocation and wall time in ms -> GB/s."""
19	    if time_ms <= 0:
20	        return 0.0
21	    return bytes_moved / (time_ms * 1e-3) / 1e9
22	
23	
24	def peak_fraction(
25	    achieved: float,
26	    peak: float,
27	) -> float:
28	    """Return achieved / peak, clamped to [0, infinity)."""
29	    if peak <= 0:
30	        return 0.0
31	    return max(0.0, achieved / peak)

1	"""Centralized GPU timing for benchmark.py files.
2	
3	All problems' benchmark.py should call `time_fn` from here so we have one
4	implementation of warmup, L2 flush, and CUDA event capture to maintain.
5	
6	Methodology:
7	  - 10 warmup calls absorb Triton autotune (typical ~7 configs) and
8	    torch.compile reduce-overhead CUDA-graph capture.
9	  - Between each timed call, `_l2_flush()` writes 128 MB to evict L2
10	    (Blackwell L2 is 96 MB; we want any prior L2 contents flushed so
11	    we measure HBM-load bandwidth, not L2-cached bandwidth).
12	  - GPU timing via cuda.Event with synchronize() AFTER record() but
13	    BEFORE elapsed_time() — the canonical NVIDIA pattern.
14	  - Reported value is the median of `iters` trials, robust to outliers.
15	
16	Notes / known biases not addressed here:
17	  - torch.compile(mode="reduce-overhead") gets CUDA graphs which eliminate
18	    launch overhead. Custom Triton/CUDA kernels do NOT get this treatment.
19	    On small shapes where launch overhead matters, this gives compile an
20	    artificial advantage. We accept this as the cost of using the agreed
21	    "compiled" baseline policy.
22	  - cuBLAS / cuDNN allocate workspaces on first call. 10 warmup absorbs.
23	  - Median over a fairly small number of trials (default 30) is fine for
24	    headline numbers but won't catch bimodal distributions. Use --extra
25	    instrumentation if you ever care.
26	"""

28	
29	import os
30	import re
31

22	def _coerce_float(x):
23	    """Accept int/float/str scientific-notation as float; pass through dicts."""
24	    if isinstance(x, (int, float)):
25	        return float(x)
26	    if isinstance(x, str):
27	        try:
28	            return float(x)
29	        except ValueError:
30	            return x
31	    return x

We can use a 1D or 2D grid of tiles. For each tile (expert, tile_m, tile_n), we compute the output block. The challenge is variable n_e per expert. One common approach is to flatten across experts: each tile belongs to an expert. We need to map tile coordinates back to (expert, row within expert). Actually, a simpler approach for grouped GEMM in Triton: - Grid: (E, cdiv(I, BLOCK_N), num_tiles_m) where num_tiles_m is max over experts of cdiv(n_e, BLOCK_M) — but experts with fewer tokens waste tiles. - Better: flatten the M dimension across all experts and use BLOCK_M tiles. Let me think. We have total T_perm rows across all experts. Each row belongs to an expert. For each output row i, we know expert = find_expert(i) via binary search on offsets. But that's expensive. Alternative: create a metadata tensor mapping each row to its expert, then use gather/scatter. But that adds memory traffic. Better: process expert by expert in a Python loop, launching one Triton kernel per expert. This avoids the variable-length complexity inside the kernel. Let me think about silu. In Triton, we can implement silu as x * tl.sigmoid(x). Sigmoid can be computed as 1 / (1 + exp(-x)) or use tl.sigmoid if available. Now, the grouped aspect. Actually, on Ampere, bf16 dot with fp32 acc uses tensor cores. One more thing: we should use GROUP_M ordering to improve L2 cache. The standard Triton matmul uses group ordering: group_id = pid // num_pid_n; group_size = ... But for our case with one expert at a time, the standard ordering might be fine. Actually, we can use the classic swizzled ordering: ```python num_pid_m = tl.cdiv(M, BLOCK_M) num_pid_n = tl.cdiv(N, BLOCK_N) num_pid_in_group = GROUP_M * num_pid_n group_id = pid // num_pid_in_group first_pid_m = group_id * GROUP_M group_size_m = min(num_pid_m - first_pid_m, GROUP_M) pid_m = first_pid_m + (pid % group_size_m) pid_n = (pid % num_pid_in_group) // group_size_m ``` This helps with memory coalescing. +++ b//home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260619_022906_kimi-claude_kimi-k2.7-code_06_sonic_moe_swiglu/repo/problems/06_sonic_moe_swiglu/solution.py

+"""Grouped GEMM + fused SwiGLU for MoE up-projection on Ampere (SM86).
+
+Per-expert Triton kernel: h_e = silu(x_e @ W_gate[e]) * (x_e @ W_up[e]).
+"""
+from __future__ import annotations
+
+import torch
+import torch.nn as nn
+import triton
+import triton.language as tl
+
+
+@triton.autotune(
+    configs=[
+        triton.Config({"BLOCK_M": 64, "BLOCK_N": 64, "BLOCK_K": 64, "GROUP_M": 8}, num_stages=3, num_warps=4),
+        triton.Config({"BLOCK_M": 64, "BLOCK_N": 128, "BLOCK_K": 64, "GROUP_M": 8}, num_stages=3, num_warps=4),
+        triton.Config({"BLOCK_M": 128, "BLOCK_N": 64, "BLOCK_K": 64, "GROUP_M": 8}, num_stages=3, num_warps=4),
+        triton.Config({"BLOCK_M": 128, "BLOCK_N": 128, "BLOCK_K": 64, "GROUP_M": 8}, num_stages=3, num_warps=8),
+        triton.Config({"BLOCK_M": 128, "BLOCK_N": 128, "BLOCK_K": 32, "GROUP_M": 8}, num_stages=4, num_warps=8),
+        triton.Config({"BLOCK_M": 64, "BLOCK_N": 128, "BLOCK_K": 32, "GROUP_M": 8}, num_stages=4, num_warps=4),
+    ],
+    key=["M", "N", "K"],
+)
+@triton.jit
+def moe_swiglu_kernel(
+    x_ptr,
+    w_gate_ptr,
+    w_up_ptr,
+    out_ptr,
+    M,
+    K,
+    N,
+    stride_xm,
+    stride_xk,
+    stride_wgk,
+    stride_wgn,
+    stride_wuk,
+    stride_wun,
+    stride_om,
+    stride_on,
+    BLOCK_M: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr,
+    BLOCK_K: tl.constexpr,
+    GROUP_M: tl.constexpr,
+):
+    """Compute one (M,N) tile of silu(x @ W_gate) * (x @ W_up)."""
+    pid = tl.program_id(0)
+    num_pid_m = tl.cdiv(M, BLOCK_M)
+    num_pid_n = tl.cdiv(N, BLOCK_N)
+    num_pid_in_group = GROUP_M * num_pid_n
+    group_id = pid // num_pid_in_group
+    first_pid_m = group_id * GROUP_M
+    group_size_m = min(num_pid_m - first_pid_m, GROUP_M)
+    pid_m = first_pid_m + (pid % group_size_m)
+    pid_n = (pid % num_pid_in_group) // group_size_m
+
+    offs_m = pid_m * BLOCK_M + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_M)
+    offs_n = pid_n * BLOCK_N + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_N)
+
+    acc_gate = tl.zeros((BLOCK_M, BLOCK_N), dtype=tl.float32)
+    acc_up = tl.zeros((BLOCK_M, BLOCK_N), dtype=tl.float32)
+
+    for k in range(0, tl.cdiv(K, BLOCK_K)):
+        offs_k = k * BLOCK_K + tl.arange(0, BLOCK_K)
+        x_ptrs = x_ptr + (offs_m[:, None] * stride_xm + offs_k[None, :] * stride_xk)
+        w_gate_ptrs = w_gate_ptr + (offs_k[:, None] * stride_wgk + offs_n[None, :] * stride_wgn)
+        w_up_ptrs = w_up_ptr + (offs_k[:, None] * stride_wuk + offs_n[None, :] * stride_wun)
+
+        mask_k = offs_k < K
+        mask_m = offs_m < M
+        x_block = tl.load(x_ptrs, mask=mask_m[:, None] & mask_k[None, :], other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+        w_gate_block = tl.load(w_gate_ptrs, mask=mask_k[:, None] & (offs_n[None, :] < N), other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+        w_up_block = tl.load(w_up_ptrs, mask=mask_k[:, None] & (offs_n[None, :] < N), other=0.0).to(tl.bfloat16)
+
+        acc_gate = tl.dot(x_block, w_gate_block, acc_gate)
+        acc_up = tl.dot(x_block, w_up_block, acc_up)
+
+    gate = acc_gate.to(tl.bfloat16)
+    up = acc_up.to(tl.bfloat16)
+
+    gate_f = gate.to(tl.float32)
+    silu = gate_f * tl.sigmoid(gate_f)
+    out = (silu * up.to(tl.float32)).to(tl.bfloat16)
+
+    out_ptrs = out_ptr + (offs_m[:, None] * stride_om + offs_n[None, :] * stride_on)
+    tl.store(out_ptrs, out, mask=(offs_m[:, None] < M) & (offs_n[None, :] < N))
+
+
+class Model(nn.Module):
+    """Up-projection of a top-K MoE FFN with fused SwiGLU.
+
+    Inputs at call time:
+      hidden_states:    (T_perm, H)  bf16, already permuted to expert order
+      expert_offsets:   (E+1,)       int32, prefix sums of token counts per expert
+    Output:
+      gated_up:         (T_perm, I)  bf16
+    """
+
+    def __init__(self, T_total: int, H: int, I: int, E: int, K: int):  # noqa: E741
+        super().__init__()
+        self.T_total = T_total
+        self.H = H
+        self.I = I
+        self.E = E
+        self.K = K
+        self.W_gate = nn.Parameter(torch.empty(E, H, I, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
+        self.W_up = nn.Parameter(torch.empty(E, H, I, dtype=torch.bfloat16))
+        nn.init.normal_(self.W_gate, std=0.02)
+        nn.init.normal_(self.W_up, std=0.02)
+
+    def forward(
+        self,
+        hidden_states: torch.Tensor,
+        expert_offsets: torch.Tensor,
+    ) -> torch.Tensor:
+        T_perm, H = hidden_states.shape
+        out = torch.empty(T_perm, self.I, dtype=torch.bfloat16, device=hidden_states.device)
+
+        for e in range(self.E):
+            start = int(expert_offsets[e].item())
+            end = int(expert_offsets[e + 1].item())
+            n_e = end - start
+            if n_e == 0:
+                continue
+
+            x_e = hidden_states[start:end]
+            W_gate_e = self.W_gate[e]
+            W_up_e = self.W_up[e]
+            out_e = out[start:end]
+
+            grid = (triton.cdiv(n_e, 128) * triton.cdiv(self.I, 128),)
+            moe_swiglu_kernel[grid](
+                x_e, W_gate_e, W_up_e, out_e,
+                n_e, H, self.I,
+                x_e.stride(0), x_e.stride(1),
+                W_gate_e.stride(0), W_gate_e.stride(1),
+                W_up_e.stride(0), W_up_e.stride(1),
+                out_e.stride(0), out_e.stride(1),
+            )
+
+        return out

import reference, solution

device='cuda'
shape = {'T_total': 4096, 'H': 2048, 'I': 1024, 'E': 64, 'K': 4}

    setattr(reference, k, v)

sol = solution.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).to(device).eval()

reasoning (10163 chars)
Performance is poor: peak_fraction 0.0409, RESULT: LOW. The memory says a good solution should get ~0.147 geomean. My per-expert Python loop with 128 kernel launches is too slow. I need to implement the single fused kernel with sync-free device-side schedule as described in the memory. Let me redesign. The working solution design from memory: - Single fused kernel, one program per (m-tile, n-tile) - Dual fp32 accumulators (gate+up) against SAME loaded x tile (x read once, both weights once) - SwiGLU fused in epilogue; one launch - BLOCK_M=128, BLOCK_N=64, BLOCK_K=64 - Tile->expert via sync-free device-side schedule: from expert_offsets build per padded m-tile slot (expert_id, row_start, row_end) with torch.searchsorted - Grid m-dim = ceil(T_perm/BM)+E (tight upper bound), padded slots early-return. So instead of a Python loop over experts, I launch one kernel with a grid covering all (m-tile, n-tile). Each m-tile is assigned to a specific expert. We need a schedule that maps m-tile index to (expert_id, row_offset_within_expert). The idea: each expert e has n_e rows, which is ceil(n_e/BLOCK_M) m-tiles. Total m-tiles = sum_e ceil(n_e/BLOCK_M). To avoid a per-expert prefix sum on CPU, we can pad each expert to ceil(n_e/BLOCK_M) tiles. The grid m-dim is at most ceil(T_perm/BLOCK_M) + E (when each expert has one extra padded row). Actually the memory says grid m-dim = ceil(T_perm/BM)+E (tight upper bound). Wait, sum_e ceil(n_e/BM) <= ceil(sum_e n_e / BM) + E = ceil(T_perm/BM) + E. Because each expert contributes at most one partial tile beyond the total count. So grid m-dim = ceil(T_perm/BM) + E. Now we need to map tile_m to (expert_id, row_start). We can precompute this mapping in __init__ or forward using torch.searchsorted. Approach for schedule: 1. Compute tiles_per_expert = ceil((offsets[1:] - offsets[:-1]) / BLOCK_M) 2. Compute tile_offsets = cumsum(tiles_per_expert) (length E+1) 3. Total tiles = tile_offsets[-1] 4. For each tile t, expert_id = searchsorted(tile_offsets, t) - 1 5. tile_within_expert = t - tile_offsets[expert_id] 6. row_start = offsets[expert_id] + tile_within_expert * BLOCK_M We can compute this mapping on CPU (since expert_offsets is small) and pass two tensors to the kernel: tile_expert (num_tiles,) int32 and tile_row_start (num_tiles,) int32. Or compute on GPU with searchsorted. The memory says "with torch.searchsorted (no .cpu()/.item() sync)". So compute on GPU. Actually, the kernel can take expert_offsets and compute the mapping per thread block. But that requires binary search per block, which is slow. Better to precompute tile_expert and tile_row_start once per forward and pass to kernel. But these are small tensors (num_tiles <= ceil(262144/128)+128 = 2176). uv run python - <<'PY'
import torch

def schedule(E, T_perm, offsets, BLOCK_M):
    counts = offsets[1:] - offsets[:-1]
    tiles_per_expert = (counts + BLOCK_M - 1) // BLOCK_M
    tile_offsets = torch.cat([torch.zeros(1, dtype=torch.int32), torch.cumsum(tiles_per_expert, dim=0)])
    grid_m = (T_perm + BLOCK_M - 1) // BLOCK_M + E
    tile_idx = torch.arange(grid_m, dtype=torch.int32)
    tile_expert = torch.searchsorted(tile_offsets, tile_idx) - 1
    tile_row_start = offsets[tile_expert] + (tile_idx - tile_offsets[tile_expert]) * BLOCK_M
    tile_expert = torch.where(tile_idx < tile_offsets[-1], tile_expert, torch.full_like(tile_expert, -1))
    return tile_offsets, tile_idx, tile_expert, tile_row_start

# small synthetic
E = 4
T_perm = 300
base = T_perm // E
counts = torch.full((E,), base, dtype=torch.int32)
counts[:T_perm - base*E] += 1
offsets = torch.zeros(E+1, dtype=torch.int32)
offsets[1:] = torch.cumsum(counts, dim=0)
print('counts', counts)
print('offsets', offsets)

BLOCK_M = 64
tile_offsets, tile_idx, tile_expert, tile_row_start = schedule(E, T_perm, offsets, BLOCK_M)
print('tile_offsets', tile_offsets)
for i in range(len(tile_idx)):
    print(i, 'expert', tile_expert[i].item(), 'row_start', tile_row_start[i].item())

import numpy as np

def schedule(E, T_perm, offsets, BLOCK_M):
    counts = offsets[1:] - offsets[:-1]
    tiles_per_expert = (counts + BLOCK_M - 1) // BLOCK_M
    tile_offsets = np.concatenate([[0], np.cumsum(tiles_per_expert)])
    grid_m = (T_perm + BLOCK_M - 1) // BLOCK_M + E
    tile_idx = np.arange(grid_m, dtype=np.int32)
    tile_expert = np.searchsorted(tile_offsets, tile_idx, side='left') - 1
    tile_row_start = offsets[tile_expert] + (tile_idx - tile_offsets[tile_expert]) * BLOCK_M
    tile_expert = np.where(tile_idx < tile_offsets[-1], tile_expert, -1)
    return tile_offsets, tile_idx, tile_expert, tile_row_start

E = 4
T_perm = 300
base = T_perm // E
counts = np.full((E,), base, dtype=np.int32)
counts[:T_perm - base*E] += 1
offsets = np.zeros(E+1, dtype=np.int32)
offsets[1:] = np.cumsum(counts)

print('offsets', offsets)

-rwxr-xr-x 1 infatoshi infatoshi 2288 Jun 19 02:29 /home/infatoshi/kernelbench.com/benchmarks/hard/outputs/runs/20260619_022906_kimi-claude_kimi-k2.7-code_06_sonic_moe_swiglu/bin/gpu-lock-exec
#!/bin/bash
set -euo pipefail
name="$1"
real="$2"
shift 2
if [ -z "$real" ]; then
    echo "$name is unavailable" >&2
    exit 127
fi
real_abs="$(readlink -f "$real" 2>/dev/null || printf '%s' "$real")"
case "$name" in
    uv)
        fallback="${REAL_UV_FALLBACK:-}"
        ;;
    python|python3)
        fallback="${REAL_PYTHON_FALLBACK:-}"
        ;;
    *)
        fallback=""
        ;;
esac
if [ -n "${RUN_DIR:-}" ] && [[ "$real_abs" == "${RUN_DIR}/bin/"* ]] && [ -n "$fallback" ]; then
    real="$fallback"
fi
if [ "${KBH_GPU_LOCK_HELD:-0}" = "1" ]; then
    exec "$real" "$@"
fi
if [ "${KBH_AGENT_PHASE:-0}" = "1" ]; then
    case "$name" in
        uv|python|python3|nvidia-smi|nvcc)
            exec "$real" "$@"
            ;;
        ncu|nsys)
            echo "$name is disabled during KernelBench parallel agent phase; official benchmarking runs under the GPU lock after generation." >&2
            exit 125
            ;;
    esac
fi
owner_file="${KBH_GPU_LOCK}.owner"
if [ -f "$owner_file" ]; then
    IFS=$'\t' read -r owner_pid owner_run_dir < "$owner_file" || true
    if [ "${owner_run_dir:-}" = "${RUN_DIR:-}" ] && kill -0 "${owner_pid:-}" 2>/dev/null; then
        exec "$real" "$@"
    fi
fi

    ref = reference.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).to(device).eval()
    sol = solution.Model(*reference.get_init_inputs()).to(device).eval()
    sol.load_state_dict(ref.state_dict(), strict=True)
    torch.manual_seed(42)
    inputs = [t.to(device) for t in reference.get_inputs()]
    with torch.no_grad():
        r = ref(*inputs)
        s = sol(*inputs)
    print(shape, 'maxdiff', (r.float()-s.float()).abs().max().item(), 'allclose', torch.allclose(r.float(), s.float(), atol=0.02, rtol=0.02))

1	"""Grouped GEMM + fused SwiGLU for MoE up-projection on Ampere (SM86).
2	
3	Single fused Triton kernel with a sync-free device-side schedule.  From
4	expert_offsets we build a per-(m-tile) slot table on the GPU; each program
5	looks up its (expert, row_start) and computes:
6	
7	    h_e = silu(x_e @ W_gate[e]) * (x_e @ W_up[e])
8	
9	The same x tile is loaded once and fed into both gate/up dots.
10	"""
11	from __future__ import annotations
12	
13	import os
14	os.environ.setdefault("PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF", "expandable_segments:True")
15	
16	import torch
17	import torch.nn as nn
18	import triton
19	import triton.language as tl
20	
21	
22	@triton.jit
23	def moe_swiglu_grouped_kernel(
24	    x_ptr,
25	    w_gate_ptr,
26	    w_up_ptr,
27	    out_ptr,
28	    expert_offsets_ptr,
29	    tile_expert_ptr,
30	    tile_row_start_ptr,
31	    grid_m,
32	    T_perm,
33	    H,
34	    I,
35	    stride_xm,
36	    stride_xk,
37	    stride_we,
38	    stride_wk,
39	    stride_wn,
40	    stride_om,
41	    stride_on,
42	    BLOCK_M: tl.constexpr,
43	    BLOCK_N: tl.constexpr,
44	    BLOCK_K: tl.constexpr,
45	    GROUP_M: tl.constexpr,
46	):
47	    """One fused (m-tile, n-tile) block of grouped GEMM + SwiGLU."""
48	    pid = tl.program_id(0)
49	    num_pid_m = grid_m
50	    num_pid_n = (I + BLOCK_N - 1) // BLOCK_N
51	    num_pid_in_group = GROUP_M * num_pid_n
52	    group_id = pid // num_pid_in_group
53	    first_pid_m = group_id * GROUP_M
54	    group_size_m = min(num_pid_m - first_pid_m, GROUP_M

assistant
Implemented `solution.py` with a single fused Triton kernel for the grouped GEMM + SwiGLU up-projection on RTX 3090 (SM86). What it does: - Builds a sync-free device-side tile schedule from `expert_offsets` using `torch.searchsorted` (no `.cpu()`/`.item()` syncs). - Launches one kernel covering all `(m-tile, n-tile)` slots; padded slots early-return via `expert == -1`. - Each block loads one `x` tile and feeds it into both gate and up `tl.dot` accumulators (fp32 acc), then fuses `silu(gate) * up` in the epilogue with bf16 round-trips matching PyTorch semantics. - Sets `PYTORCH_CUDA_ALLOC_CONF=expandable_segments:True` at import time to avoid the `check.py` OOM fragmentation issue on the 24 GB card. Verified: - `uv run python check.py` → `PASS` - `uv run python benchmark.py` → `peak_fraction: 0.1610`, `RESULT: OK` Per-shape results: - shape 0 (32K/4096/1536/128/8): 9.54 TFLOPS, 0.1344 peak fraction - shape 1 (4K/2048/1024/64/4): 16.43 TFLOPS, 0.2314 peak fraction - shape 2 (16K/2048/4096/64/8): 9.53 TFLOPS, 0.1342 peak fraction Tuned config: `BLOCK_M=128`, `BLOCK_N=64`, `BLOCK_K=64`, `GROUP_M=8`, `num_warps=4`, `num_stages=2`.
